# REPO-004 Root Surface Classification Audit

Report ID: REPO-004
Status: ARCHITECTURE DISCOVERY
Subject: Repository root surface classification before physical migration
Decision State: ROOT IS MIXED SURFACE / PLATFORM ASSUMPTION REJECTED

---

## 1. Executive Verdict

The repository root is not a pure Platform surface.

The root currently contains a mixture of constitutional governance, architecture documentation, active runtime entrypoints, CRMAddlife-branded PWA shell assets, transitional Forge engines, root-level tests, historical reports and unknown artifacts.

Final classification:

- True Forge Core: governance, constitution, architecture and documented Forge decision assets.
- Transitional Forge: root-level engines/tests that may be active but are not yet physically assigned to domains.
- CRMAddlife Legacy: files with observable CRM Addlife branding, current PWA shell evidence or direct app-shell compatibility evidence.
- Unknown: files whose owner/origin cannot be proven from observable evidence in this audit.

Constitutional conclusion:

> Root is a protected compatibility and governance surface, not a destination domain.

---

## 2. Miranda Evidence Standard

This audit rejects classification based only on memory, assumption or naming.

Accepted evidence types:

- File content evidence, such as `CRM Addlife` strings or compatibility comments.
- Import evidence, such as `app.js` importing root route modules.
- Runtime evidence, such as `index.html` loading `app.js`, `manifest.json` and `service-worker.js`.
- Reference evidence, such as files mentioning root runtime assets.
- Git history evidence where available.

Important limit:

Git history for `app.js`, `manifest.json`, `service-worker.js` and `index.html` shows first appearance in the `Forge OS Initial Architecture Snapshot`. That proves they entered this repository snapshot; it does not prove whether they were authored before Forge or within Forge.

## 4. CRMAddlife Legacy Evidence Findings

| File | Observable Evidence | Audit Finding |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `manifest.json` | `name: CRM Addlife`, `short_name: Addlife` | Strong CRMAddlife branding evidence; still required by `index.html` manifest link. |
| `index.html` | `title: CRM Addlife Professional`, header text `CRM Addlife`, loads `app.js`, `manifest.json`, registers `service-worker.js` | Strong CRMAddlife-branded PWA shell evidence; active runtime entrypoint. |
| `app.js` | Imports root route modules; exposes `window.supabaseClient` as compatibility global for legacy modules; logs `APP V7 ENTERPRISE` | Active transitional app shell with explicit compatibility layer evidence. |
| `service-worker.js` | Loaded by `index.html`; imports `/sw-cache-config.js` | Active offline runtime; CRMAddlife inheritance not proven by content, but tied to current PWA shell. |
| `sw-cache-config.js` | Caches `/`, `/index.html`, `/styles.css`, `/app.js` | Active compatibility/runtime asset for current PWA shell. |
| `dashboard.js` / `design-system-preview.html` | Contain `CRM Addlife` strings | CRMAddlife-branded UI evidence. |

---

## 6. Platform Boundary Definition

Platform owns generic runtime capability:

- App shell mechanics.
- Runtime bootstrapping.
- Storage and sync infrastructure.
- Event bus and module lifecycle.
- Offline/cache capability.
- Command execution infrastructure.
- Authentication plumbing when it is generic infrastructure.

Platform does not own:

- Advisor decisions.
- Manager allocation decisions.
- Product truth.
- Policy operational truth.
- Compensation or contest logic.
- Rule Pack interpretation.
- Governance documents.
- Historical reports.
- Any file merely because it is hard to classify.

Boundary verdict:

> Platform is not a bucket for everything that does not fit. Platform owns runtime capability only.

---

## 7. Root Governance Model

Recommended future-state root model:

D. Runtime entrypoints plus constitutional/governance anchors only.

Allowed root classes:

1. Runtime entrypoints that hosting, browser or package/runtime conventions require at root.
2. Constitutional anchors such as `AGENTS.md`, constitution and build tree until a governance ADR changes their location.
3. Compatibility shims with explicit expiration plans.
4. Minimal repository metadata such as `.gitignore` and deployment redirects.

Disallowed as permanent root residents:

- Domain engines.
- Master tests.
- Discovery reports.
- Product/rule documentation.
- Unknown artifacts.
- Legacy compatibility files without exit criteria.

---

## 8. Migration Impact Assessment

Root movement is high risk because root currently acts as:

- Browser/PWA entrypoint surface.
- Legacy compatibility surface.
- Governance surface.
- Temporary engine/test staging surface.
- Historical document archive.

Do not move root runtime files until a runtime reference scanner and browser/PWA validation path exist.

Do not move root governance files until ADR-0020 or a dedicated governance ADR explicitly says root governance anchors may move.

---

## 11. Relocation Candidates

| Candidate Class | Rule |
| --- | --- |
| Governance anchors | Remain root until governance ADR; eventual `docs/governance/` only if tooling knows where to find them. |
| Architecture / documentation reports | Candidate for `docs/` consolidation after docs inventory and link scan. |
| Domain engines | Candidate for domain folders only after owner registry and import dry-run. |
| Tests | Candidate for `tests/` only after test gate map. |
| CRMAddlife runtime shell | Do not move until runtime/PWA migration plan exists. |
| Unknown artifacts | Legacy quarantine review; no deletion without evidence. |

---

## 12. Final Verdict

The assumption that all root files are Platform assets is rejected.

Final classification:

- True Forge Core: constitutional and architecture governance assets.
- Transitional Forge: active root-level Forge engines/tests awaiting domain ownership and dry-run migration.
- CRMAddlife Legacy: observable CRMAddlife-branded or PWA shell compatibility files.
- Unknown: files without enough evidence for owner/origin classification.

Root governance rule:

> Repository root may contain runtime entrypoints and constitutional/governance anchors only. Everything else is transitional until ownership, dependency and rollback evidence proves a destination.
